> 2, yes, 3 yes... I would like your honest opinion on 1 though on what you     
  think would actually look better and what feels smoother.. I mean listen,

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Honest opinion: keep the cards. Here's why:

  The cards aren't just decorative вҖ” they create clear visual boundaries between
   "what I need to fill in" vs "what the system calculated for me." Stream Info
  + Products Sold = their input. Calculation Breakdown = system output.
  Adjustments = optional input. Inventory = optional input.

  Without cards, all that bleeds together and it gets harder to scan "where am
  I?" especially on a form this long. Compared to a Google Sheet where
  everything is a flat grid of cells with no visual hierarchy, the cards are
  already a massive upgrade.

  The one thing I would do is tighten up the spacing between cards so it feels
  more like one flowing form rather than separate disconnected blocks. But I
  wouldn't remove them entirely.

  Let me just do the rename and leave the cards as-is.

  stream, there might not be a payout record yet.

  Go to /streamdata/admin/payouts and check вҖ” do you see anything there? If it's
   empty, it's because the system currently creates payout records per-week, not
   per-stream. We might need to either:

  1. Auto-create a payout record when a stream is submitted
  2. Add a "Generate Payouts" button on the admin side that tallies up the
  week's streams into a payout record

  Which makes more sense for your workflow? Do you pay streamers per-stream or
  per-week?

> no its per week, ok so i wont know what that looks like until Monday morning  
  comes?                                                                        

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Right now it won't auto-generate on Monday вҖ” there's no automation for that
  yet. The payout records need to be created somehow. Options:

  1. Manual button: You click "Generate Weekly Payouts" on the admin payouts
  page when you're ready to pay (Monday/Tuesday). It tallies up all submitted
  streams for that week across all streamers and creates the payout records.
  2. Auto-generate on week close: When a new week starts (Monday), the system
  automatically closes the previous week and generates payout records.

  For now, option 1 is simpler and gives you control вҖ” you hit the button when
  you're ready, review the numbers, then mark as paid. Want me to add that?

в—Ҹ Done. Here's what's new:

  "Generate Weekly Payouts" button on the admin payouts page
  (/streamdata/admin/payouts):
  - Click it to tally all submitted streams from completed weeks
  - Creates payout records per streamer per week
  - Closes the weekly period so no more streams can be added to it
  - Shows how many records were generated
  - Won't create duplicates if you click it again

  The flow now:
  1. Streamers submit streams throughout the week (Mon-Sun)
  2. Monday/Tuesday you go to All Payouts вҶ’ click "Generate Weekly Payouts"
  3. Review the numbers
  4. Click "Mark as Paid" on each one (or "Mark All as Paid")

   a payout record for that test stream you submitted.

> nope didn't work.... literally the only thing that works after it puts you in 
   the portal with no sidebar is a quick refresh and then it puts you into the  
  normal portal with the sidebars and everything... Is there not some type of   
  like fix there why does it do that?                                           

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  OK so the sidebar DOES show after a refresh вҖ” that means force-dynamic is
  working on the second request, but the FIRST request after login still serves
  the stale version. This is a caching/redirect issue, not a layout issue.

  The problem is the login flow: after login, router.push('/streamdata') does a
  client-side navigation which uses the React Server Component cache from the
  initial page load (when you weren't authenticated). The refresh works because
  it's a full server request with the new session cookie.

  The fix is dead simple вҖ” use window.location.href instead of router.push so it
   does a full page navigation with the cookie:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

в—Ҹ Update(app\(portal)\streamdata\login\page.tsx)
  вҺҝ В Added 3 lines, removed 3 lines

         -tsx                                                            
      43 -        // checks the role and redirects to admin or dashboard 
         -accordingly                                                    
      44 -        router.push('/streamdata')                             
      42 +        // Full page navigation (not client-side) so the server
         + reads                                                         
      43 +        // the fresh session cookie and renders the layout with
         + sidebar                                                       
      44 +        window.location.href = '/streamdata'                   
      45        }
      46      } catch {
      47        setError('Something went wrong. Please try again.')

      197 +                                                              
      198 +    const { id, name, manufacturer, year } = parsed.data      
      199 +                                                              
      200 +    const [updated] = await db                                
      201 +      .update(products)                                       
      202 +      .set({ name, manufacturer: manufacturer || null, year: y
          +ear || null })                                                
      203 +      .where(eq(products.id, id))                             
      204 +      .returning({                                            
      205 +        id: products.id,                                      
      206 +        name: products.name,                                  
      207 +        manufacturer: products.manufacturer,                  
      208 +        year: products.year,                                  
      209 +        isActive: products.isActive,                          
      210 +      })                                                      
      211 +                                                              
      212 +    if (!updated) {                                           
      213 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Product not found' },
          + { status: 404 })                                             
      214 +    }                                                         
      215 +                                                              
      216 +    return NextResponse.json({ product: updated })            
      217 +  } catch (err) {                                             
      218 +    const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Unkn
          +own error'                                                    
      219 +    console.error('PUT /api/streamdata/admin/products error:',
          + message)                                                     
      220 +    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Failed to update produc
          +t' }, { status: 500 })                                        
      221 +  }                                                           
      222 +}                                                             
      223 +                                                              
      224 +export async function DELETE(request: NextRequest) {          
      225 +  try {                                                       
      226 +    const { error } = await requireAdmin()                    
      227 +    if (error) return error                                   
      228 +                                                              
      229 +    const ip = getClientIp(request)                           
      230 +    const limit = rateLimit(ip, { maxRequests: 15, windowMs: 6
          +0000 })                                                       
      231 +    if (!limit.success) {                                     
      232 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Too many requests' },
          + { status: 429 })                                             
      233 +    }                                                         
      234 +                                                              
      235 +    const body = await request.json()                         
      236 +    const parsed = deleteProductSchema.safeParse(body)        
      237 +                                                              
      238 +    if (!parsed.success) {                                    
      239 +      return NextResponse.json(                               
      240 +        { error: parsed.error.issues[0]?.message || 'Invalid i
          +nput' },                                                      
      241 +        { status: 400 }                                       
      242 +      )                                                       
      243 +    }                                                         
      244 +                                                              
      245 +    const { id } = parsed.data                                
      246 +                                                              
      247 +    const [deleted] = await db                                
      248 +      .delete(products)                                       
      249 +      .where(eq(products.id, id))                             
      250 +      .returning({ id: products.id, name: products.name })    
      251 +                                                              
      252 +    if (!deleted) {                                           
      253 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Product not found' },
          + { status: 404 })                                             
      254 +    }                                                         
      255 +                                                              
      256 +    return NextResponse.json({ deleted: true, product: deleted
          + })                                                           
      257 +  } catch (err) {                                             
      258 +    const message = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Unkn
          +own error'                                                    
      259 +    console.error('DELETE /api/streamdata/admin/products error
          +:', message)                                                  
      260 +    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Failed to delete produc
          +t' }, { status: 500 })                                        
      261 +  }                                                           
      262 +}

в—Ҹ OK this is actually a really well-thought-out two-tier pricing model. Let me
  make sure I understand it:

  Two cost layers:
  - Owner COGS (what Chicken paid): $180/box вҖ” only admins see this
  - Breaker COGS (what the breaker's cost is): $205/box вҖ” this is what breakers
  see and what their payout is calculated from

  So when admin adds inventory:
  - 10 cases of Chrome Hobby @ $180 (owner cost) вҶ’ assign breaker price of $205
  - Later: 5 more cases @ $210 (owner cost) вҶ’ assign breaker price of $225

  Each entry is a separate lot with its own owner cost AND breaker cost. The
  admin sees both, the breaker only sees their cost.

  For the admin dashboard, we show:
  - Average owner COGS across all lots of that product
  - Total owner cost invested
  - Margin between owner cost and breaker cost (the markup)

  Here's my proposed data model:

  inventory_lots (admin adds these)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ product_id (which product)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ quantity (how many boxes/cases received)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ unit_type (case/box/pack)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ owner_cost_per_unit ($180 вҖ” admin eyes only)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ breaker_cost_per_unit ($205 вҖ” what breakers see as their COGS)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ quantity_remaining (decrements as breakers sell)
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ received_date
  в”ңв”Җв”Җ notes ("Release day batch", "Second order", etc.)

  When breaker submits a stream:
  - They pick a product from dropdown (only shows in-stock products)
  - System auto-fills the breaker cost from the most recent lot's
  breaker_cost_per_unit
  - Quantity sold deducts from quantity_remaining (FIFO вҖ” oldest lot first)

  The breaker never sees $180. They see $205 as their cost. Your P/L tracks both
   layers вҖ” you know your true margin.

  Does this match what you're thinking?

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  OK let me think through this with you because you're raising a real problem.

  The core issue: breaker cost is fluid and can't always be determined at the 
  time inventory comes in.

  Here's what I think the right approach is:

  Admin side (Stock Management):
  - Owner cost per case/box is required вҖ” you always know what you paid
  - Breaker cost is optional вҖ” set it when you know it, leave it blank when you
  don't
  - Auto-calculate owner cost per box from case cost (and vice versa) so the
  math is done for you
  - Breaker cost can be updated later at any time as pricing solidifies
  - When breaker cost is set, it auto-populates into the breaker's dropdown.
  When it's not set, the breaker enters their own COGS manually like they do
  now.

  Breaker side (Submit Stream):
  - If the product has a breaker cost set in inventory вҶ’ auto-fill but still
  editable (they can override)
  - If no breaker cost is set вҶ’ blank, they enter it themselves (like the Google
   Sheet)
  - Either way, the breaker always has the final say on what their COGS is

  This way:
  1. Early pre-orders: admin enters owner cost, skips breaker cost. Breakers
  enter their own COGS.
  2. Once pricing is firm: admin sets breaker cost, it auto-fills for breakers
  going forward.
  3. Price changes: admin updates breaker cost on the lot (or adds a new lot at
  new price). Old lot keeps old price.

  The inventory deduction still works regardless вҖ” it tracks units sold, and the
   COGS used comes from whatever the breaker entered (auto-filled or manual).

  Does this solve it?

в—Ҹ Crystal clear. Here's what I'm building:

  Live Break Tracker вҖ” a standalone real-time tool for breakers during their
  stream:

  1. Go Live вҖ” breaker hits a button, starts a live session
  2. Per Break Entry (repeatable throughout the stream):
    - Products in the break (e.g. 1x NBA Prizm $280, 1x Chrome $450)
    - Total COGS for the break
    - Number of spots sold (30, 32, 15, etc.)
    - Sales total (money in from the live stream counter)

в—Ҹ That's a full business strategy panel breakdown. The key takeaways:

  The opportunity is real. No competitor exists for this niche. You built it for
   yourself which is the strongest validation.

  Biggest insight: You're not building "card breaking software" вҖ” you're
  building financial operations for live commerce teams. Breaking is the
  beachhead, not the ceiling.

  Immediate next steps if you want to pursue this:
  1. Get 10-20 break groups using it (not just Chicken) to validate
  2. Make the Live Break Tracker free as a viral hook вҖ” breakers show it on
  stream
  3. Charge $79-149/mo per group for the full suite
  4. Partner with Whatnot early before they build it themselves

  Your moat: Data gravity. Once a group has 6 months of payout history and tax
  records in your system, they're not leaving.

  Your risk: The market staying too small. The expansion to mystery boxes, live
  selling, consignment houses is where the real scale lives.

  Pretty wild for something that started as "can we replace the Google Sheets?"

в—Ҹ The issue is the FK constraint вҖ” when a product has been used in stream

в—Ҹ deep-research-agent(Deep research SaaS architecture + data liability)
  вҺҝ В Done (28 tool uses В· 66.3k tokens В· 8m 49s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

в—Ҹ Here's the executive summary:

  The Recommended Path

  Architecture: Shared Database + Supabase Row-Level Security
  - Add a tenant_id column to every table
  - Supabase RLS policies enforce data isolation at the database level
  - Single Vercel deployment serves everyone
  - Cost: ~$45-120/mo for up to 100 tenants (vs $2,500+/mo for separate
  databases)

  Data Liability: You're fine
  - Sales numbers and payout data are NOT regulated (no PCI, HIPAA, SOX)
  - Only real PII is emails/names вҖ” standard SaaS stuff
  - Get a lawyer to write ToS + Privacy Policy + DPA for $500-1,500
  - Structure as "tool provider" вҖ” you provide the software, they own their data
  - Skip SOC 2 entirely вҖ” nobody in this market will ask for it
  - Don't build an admin panel that lets you browse tenant data (then you
  literally can't see it)

  Security: Practical approach
  - Supabase handles encryption at rest and in transit
  - RLS policies ensure tenants can never see each other's data
  - Put tenant context in JWT tokens
  - No need for per-tenant encryption keys вҖ” that's overkill for sales figures

  Pricing Tiers:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  That's the problem then. Resend needs a verified sending domain to send
  outbound emails. If you only set it up for receiving (inbound), it can't send.

  4. Resend will give you DNS records to add (SPF, DKIM, possibly DMARC)

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  1. Go to https://dcc.godaddy.com/ вҶ’ find chicken1of1.com вҶ’ DNS вҶ’ Manage
  2. Add these 3 records:

  Record 1 вҖ” DKIM (TXT)
  - Type: TXT
  - Name: resend._domainkey
  - Value: Copy the full value from Resend (starts with p=MIG...)
  - TTL: Default/Auto

  Record 2 вҖ” SPF (MX)
  - Type: MX
  - Name: send
  - Value: feedback-smtp.us-east-1.amazonses.com
  - Priority: 10
  - TTL: Default/Auto

  Record 3 вҖ” SPF (TXT)
  - Type: TXT
  - Name: send
  - Value: Copy the full value from Resend (starts with v=spf1 include:...)
  - TTL: Default/Auto

  After adding all 3, go back to Resend and click "Verify DNS Records". It
  usually takes a few minutes to propagate.

> OOOOKKKKK I got into Godaddy finally!                                         

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Let's go! Add these 3 DNS records:

  1. TXT Record (DKIM)
  - Type: TXT
  - Name: resend._domainkey
  - Value: Copy the full value from Resend (the long p=MIG... string)
  - TTL: Default

  2. MX Record (SPF)
  - Type: MX
  - Name: send
  - Value: feedback-smtp.us-east-1.amazonses.com
  - Priority: 10
  - TTL: Default

  3. TXT Record (SPF)
  - Type: TXT
  - Name: send
  - Value: Copy the full value from Resend (starts with v=spf1 include:...)
  - TTL: Default

  After all 3 are added, go back to Resend and hit "Verify DNS Records". Let me
  know when it says verified.

      170 +export async function DELETE(request: NextRequest) {          
      171 +  try {                                                       
      172 +    const { error } = await requireAdmin()                    
      173 +    if (error) return error                                   
      174 +                                                              
      175 +    const ip = getClientIp(request)                           
      176 +    const limit = rateLimit(ip, { maxRequests: 10, windowMs: 6
          +0000 })                                                       
      177 +    if (!limit.success) {                                     
      178 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Too many requests' },
          + { status: 429 })                                             
      179 +    }                                                         
      180 +                                                              
      181 +    const body = await request.json()                         
      182 +    const id = body?.id                                       
      183 +    if (!id || typeof id !== 'string') {                      
      184 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid user ID' }, {
          + status: 400 })                                               
      185 +    }                                                         
      186 +                                                              
      187 +    // Can't delete admin accounts                            
      188 +    const user = await db.query.users.findFirst({ where: eq(us
          +ers.id, id) })                                                
      189 +    if (!user) return NextResponse.json({ error: 'User not fou
          +nd' }, { status: 404 })                                       
      190 +    if (user.role === 'admin') {                              
      191 +      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Cannot delete admin a
          +ccounts' }, { status: 403 })                                  
      192 +    }                                                         
      193 +                                                              
      194 +    // Check if breaker has any stream submissions            
      195 +    const [submissions] = await db                            
      196 +      .select({ value: count() })                             
      197 +      .from(streamEntries)                                    
      198 +      .where(eq(streamEntries.userId, id))                    
      199 +                                                              
      200 +    if ((submissions?.value ?? 0) > 0) {                      
      201 +      return NextResponse.json({                              
      202 +        error: 'This breaker has stream submissions on record 
          +and cannot be deleted. Deactivate them instead to preserve his
          +torical data.',                                               
      203 +      }, { status: 409 })                                     
      204 +    }

          +n user

          +fig.userId, id))                                              
      208 +    await db.delete(inviteTokens).where(eq(inviteTokens.userId
          +, id))

      210 +                                                              
      211 +    return NextResponse.json({ deleted: true })

          +own error'

в—Ҹ Done and pushed. Here's how it works:

  - Active breaker вҶ’ only Deactivate option (no delete)
  - Deactivated breaker with no submissions вҶ’ Delete button shows (permanent
  removal)
  - Deactivated breaker with submissions вҶ’ API blocks deletion, tells you to
  keep them deactivated for records
  - Admin accounts вҶ’ can't be deactivated or deleted

  Keeps the portal clean while preserving historical data.

  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Meanwhile your revenue at 100 tenants averaging $90/mo each = $9,000/mo. So
  you're pocketing ~$8,643/mo. That's the 96% gross margin.

  ToS/Privacy/DPA вҖ” one-time cost. You pay a lawyer $500-1,500 once to review
  template documents. The $42/mo in the table is just that one-time cost spread
  across 12 months ($500 / 12 = ~$42). After year one it drops to $0.

  Break even at 2 customers:
  - Your fixed costs are ~$47/mo (Supabase $25 + Vercel $20 + domain $2)
  - Two customers on the Team plan = 2 Г— $79 = $158/mo revenue
  - $158 - $47 = $111 profit
  - Even two Solo customers (2 Г— $29 = $58) almost covers it

  So literally the moment you get 2 paying groups, the platform pays for itself.
   Everything after that is profit minus Stripe's 3.6% cut.

  The real question is getting those first 10-20 groups to validate demand
  before building multi-tenancy. Want to talk strategy for that?

> So basically what we want to do for multi-tenant is for every break group     
  they get their own custom domain and own backend/logins kinda like what we    
  did for chicken1of1 except we're not building a frontend webpage, right? Is   
  that what the whole vercel/domain part is about?                              

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Not exactly. The whole point of the recommended architecture (Option A) is
  that you DON'T spin up a separate backend for each group. Everyone shares ONE
  app, ONE database, ONE Vercel deployment. That's why it's so cheap.

  Here's how it works:

  One app, many tenants:
  - Your app lives at streamdata.app (or whatever domain you pick)
  - Each group gets a subdomain: chicken1of1.streamdata.app,
  breakerbros.streamdata.app, pullwax.streamdata.app
  - They all hit the same Vercel deployment, same database
  - The middleware reads the subdomain, figures out which tenant it is, and
  Supabase's Row-Level Security ensures each group can ONLY see their own data

  From the breaker's perspective:
  - They go to breakerbros.streamdata.app/login
  - They see BreakBros' logo and name (not Chicken1of1)
  - They log in, submit streams, see payouts вҖ” exactly like the Chicken portal
  - They have zero idea they're sharing infrastructure with anyone else

  Enterprise tier ($249/mo) only:
  - Custom domain like portal.breakerbros.com instead of the subdomain
  - Just a DNS CNAME pointing to Vercel вҖ” no extra deployment needed

  So there's no frontend website being built for anyone. It's your portal
  product with their branding on it. One codebase, one deployment, one database
  with row-level isolation. That's why it costs $45/mo to run 10 groups instead
  of $450/mo if you were spinning up separate instances for each.

  Make sense?

  Some thoughts on naming:

  What makes a good SaaS name for this:
  - Short, memorable
  - Implies what it does (breaks, streams, cards, live commerce)
  - Sounds like a tool/platform, not a person or shop
  - Available as a .com or .app

  "BreakerOS" is actually fire вҖ” it immediately tells you it's an operating
  system for breakers. The "OS" suffix is trendy in SaaS (LinearOS, RailwayOS
  vibe) and implies it's the backbone of your operation.

  Some variations to think about:
  - BreakerOS вҖ” clean, direct, memorable
  - BreakStack вҖ” implies a full stack of tools
  - StreamLedger вҖ” financial tracking for streams
  - BreakRoom вҖ” where breakers work (but might be taken)
  - CardOps вҖ” operations for card businesses

  what's available?

вң» Baked for 35s

> interesting, so breakeros.com is available according to Ionos, breakeros.app  
  is also, i can get breakeros.com for $1 for the first year but .app is $12    
  how come .app is more expensive                                               

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  The $1 is a promo price вҖ” GoDaddy/IONOS do that to hook you in, then renewal
  is usually $15-20/yr. The .app is $12 because Google owns the .app TLD and
  doesn't do the bait-and-switch pricing вҖ” it's a flat rate.

  For a SaaS product, .app is actually better because:
  - It signals "this is an application" not a random website
  - It requires HTTPS by default (Google enforces it)
  - It's what other modern SaaS tools use
  - No one will confuse it with a blog or landing page

  But honestly, grab both. breakeros.com for $1 and breakeros.app for $12 вҖ”
  that's $13 total. Use .app as the primary product domain and .com redirects to
   it. Protects the brand either way.

  BreakerOS is a solid name. Short, memorable, tells you exactly what it is. I'd
   lock it in before someone else does.

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Easy вҖ” once they manually set a team's price, it becomes "locked." The lock
  means it won't get auto-adjusted when other teams re-balance. Only the
  unlocked teams spread evenly.

  So the flow is:

  1. Enter COGS: $2,400
  2. Select NBA (30 teams)
  3. All 30 teams auto-fill at $80 each ($2,400 / 30)
  4. They lock Spurs at $200 вҖ” now remaining $2,200 splits across 29 unlocked
  teams = $75.86 each
  5. They lock Lakers at $150 вҖ” now remaining $2,050 splits across 28 unlocked
  teams = $73.21 each
  6. And so on

  Each team row has a small lock/unlock icon. Locked teams keep their price,
  unlocked teams auto-balance the remainder.

  Plus the margin calculator on top вҖ” they set their target margin and the whole
   thing scales up proportionally.

  Want me to build this?

вң» Cooked for 58s

> Also, lets get rid of the cent thing and round up/down idk if we should keep  
  that because for any of these platforms there is no by cent sales or anything 
   its always to the dollar so maybe we round up or have both round up and      
  down? I'm not sure what the better option would be, whats your opinion on     
  that? Do we just keep the cents for the visual for everyone or we just round  
  everything up to the dollar                                                   

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Round up to the nearest dollar. Here's why:

  - No platform supports cent pricing
  - Rounding down means you might not hit your target revenue
  - Rounding up means you make slightly MORE than your target вҖ” nobody complains
   about extra profit
  - Cleaner to read ($153 vs $152.87)

  The only thing to note is that rounding up 30 teams by even $0.50 each adds
  $15 to total revenue. The summary should show the actual total after rounding
  so they see the real numbers.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  margin%)

в—Ҹ Web Search("free sports team logo API NBA NFL MLB NHL SVG PNG CDN 2026")
  вҺҝ В Did 1 search in 8s

в—Ҹ Here's the deal on logos:

  ESPN has a public CDN that hosts all team logos and doesn't require an API
  key. The URLs follow a predictable pattern:
  - NBA: https://a.espncdn.com/i/teamlogos/nba/500/{team-abbr}.png
  - NFL: https://a.espncdn.com/i/teamlogos/nfl/500/{team-abbr}.png
  - MLB: https://a.espncdn.com/i/teamlogos/mlb/500/{team-abbr}.png
  - NHL: https://a.espncdn.com/i/teamlogos/nhl/500/{team-abbr}.png

  These are publicly accessible, no API key needed, and they're already used by
  tons of apps. I can map every team to its abbreviation and we get logos for
  free.

  For the Whatnot CSV вҖ” show me what format they expect and I'll build the
  export to match. Do you have an example or can you pull one from Whatnot?

  Sources:
  - https://a.espncdn.com/i/teamlogos/nba/500/bos.png
  - https://sportslogos.net/
  - https://www.balldontlie.io/
  - https://www.figma.com/community/file/1313826283725561022/all-sports-logo-pac
  k-v0-2

в—Ҹ Here's the fresh eyes analysis вҖ” ranked by real impact:

  1. Product Quick-Select + Cost Auto-Fill (LOW effort, daily impact)
  - Breakers pick the same products every stream. Auto-fill cost from inventory,
   add a "Repeat Last Stream" button, favorite products pinned to top of
  dropdown.
  - Some of this is partially built вҖ” inventory cost data is already being
  passed to the form.

  2. Auto-Save Drafts + Edit Submissions (LOW-MED effort)
  - Draft status exists in the schema but isn't being used for auto-persistence.
   Breakers lose work if they close the tab.
  - Allow editing submitted streams within 24-48 hours (before week closes).

  3. Live Tracker вҶ’ Submission Bridge (MED effort, kills double-entry)
  - A breaker who uses the Live Tracker during their stream then has to RE-ENTER
   the same data in the submit form. That's the same info twice.
  - "Convert to Stream Submission" button at end of live session that pre-fills
  everything.

  4. Notifications + "Who Hasn't Submitted" (MED effort)
  - No notification system at all right now. Admin has to manually check if
  breakers submitted.
  - Email reminders, payout notifications, admin dashboard widget showing who's
  missing.

  5. Whatnot API/CSV Auto-Import (HIGH effort but the dream)
  - Eliminates manual data entry entirely. Depends on whether Whatnot has a
  seller API.

  The panel's honest take: Fix the input friction first (items 1-3) before
  adding more analytics or features. The portal's biggest gap isn't insight вҖ”
  it's how tedious it is to enter data after every stream.

  Which one do you want to tackle?

в—Ҹ Popcorn Playa

  Yeah вҖ” right now if a breaker uses the Live Tracker during their stream, they
  track all their products, COGS, spots, and revenue per break in real-time.
  Then when the stream ends, they have to go to Submit Stream and re-enter all
  that same information again manually. That's the same data typed twice.

  The fix: when they end a live session, add a "Convert to Stream Submission"
  button that pre-fills the submit form with everything from the live session:

  - Stream date вҶ’ from the session's startedAt
  - Platform вҶ’ from the session's platform
  - Products sold вҶ’ aggregated from all breaks (combine duplicate products, sum
  quantities)
  - Total sales вҶ’ sum of all break revenues
  - Order count вҶ’ sum of all spots sold
  - COGS вҶ’ already calculated

  The breaker just reviews, adds their inventory in hand, and hits submit. Saves
   them 10-15 minutes of re-entering data they already tracked.

  Want me to build it?

  1. Breaker ends live session вҶ’ "Convert to Stream Submission" button
  2. Pre-fills everything from the live tracker data

  4. The products sold are pre-filled but they can add more (for any percys/side

  5. Order count also stays editable вҖ” enter the real number from the platform

  That way the live tracker data is a head start, not the final answer. The
  actual platform numbers are always the source of truth for the payout
  calculation.

  OK I think I understand now. Let me make sure I have this right:

  The ideal flow:

  1. Stock Management = the master system. All product comes in here with cost
  tracking. When a breaker sells something, it deducts from here. This is the
  source of truth for "what do we own and what did it cost."
  2. Product Management = just a catalog/database of all products that exist.

  - A) The Stock Management deductions (system tracks it automatically вҖ” breaker
   sold X from lot Y, so they must have Z remaining)
  - B) The breaker's self-reported Inventory In Hand from their latest
  submission (what they say they have)
  - C) Both вҖ” system calculates what they should have, breaker reports what they
   actually have, and you see discrepancies

  I'm guessing C is the dream but A or B is the practical starting point. Which
  one matters more to you right now?
